=== Root Cause Analysis ===

SUMMARY:
The system was temporarily degraded between 18:00‚Äì18:15 (CST), affecting three key services. Three root causes were identified, all linked to internal processing delays rather than external failures. The main impact was increased response times in configuration and order handling services.

### Root Cause Report
| Node / Service | Evidence | RootCause | Impact | Recommended Actions |
|----------------|----------|-----------|--------|---------------------|
| ts-config-service | High internal latency despite normal network performance | üîç CPU overload from inefficient code | Slower configuration responses | üõ†Ô∏è Optimize code and adjust thread settings |
| ts-order-service | CPU usage spiked to 100.5% with no errors logged | üîç CPU overload due to heavy processing | Request processing delays | üõ†Ô∏è Scale up immediately and review recent code changes |
| ts-order-other-service | High internal event delays with minimal CPU rise | üîç Inefficient event handling logic | Delayed internal task processing | üõ†Ô∏è Review event loop setup and fix any blocking operations |

*Data analyzed from system metrics and traces over the last inspection window. View the full evidence chain and detailed metrics in the right panel for the complete analysis report! üìä*

DETAILED REPORT:
# üîç Root Cause Analysis Report: Application Latency Anomalies (2025-10-14T18:00‚Äì18:15+08:00)

---

## üö® **Root Cause Identification** üîç

### üîß ts-config-service  
- **Failure occurrence time**: 2025-10-14 18:00‚Äì18:15  
- **Root cause component**: `ts-config-service` (Application)  
- **Root cause**: ‚ö†Ô∏è **CPU contention and event loop (epoll) saturation** leading to high internal processing latency, despite no external network or downstream failures.  
- **Key anomalies**:  
  - üö® High CPU thread latency (10.61% of threads affected)  
  - ‚è±Ô∏è Severe epoll event loop delays (79.41% of threads impacted)  
  - üîÑ Run queue scheduling delays (12.67% of threads delayed)  
  - üíæ Minor file I/O latency in isolated threads  

> Despite clean logs and successful traces, internal system-level resource pressure is degrading response performance.

---

### üîß ts-order-service  
- **Failure occurrence time**: 2025-10-14 18:00‚Äì18:15  
- **Root cause component**: `ts-order-service` (Application)  
- **Root cause**: ‚ö†Ô∏è **Near-total CPU saturation (100.5%) causing scheduling and I/O bottlenecks**, with secondary impact on file operations and event handling.  
- **Key anomalies**:  
  - üö® CPU usage spiked from 18% ‚Üí **100.5%**  
  - ‚è±Ô∏è epoll latency in 55.56% of threads  
  - üîÑ Run queue delays in 40% of threads ‚Äî strong sign of CPU starvation  
  - üíæ File I/O latency increased in 38.46% of operations  

> The service is overwhelmed by compute load, not request volume ‚Äî likely due to inefficient processing or sudden computational burst.

---

### üîß ts-order-other-service  
- **Failure occurrence time**: 2025-10-14 18:00‚Äì18:15  
- **Root cause component**: `ts-order-other-service` (Application)  
- **Root cause**: ‚ö†Ô∏è **Event-driven processing bottleneck (epoll)** under moderate CPU pressure, causing internal latency without external failure.  
- **Key anomalies**:  
  - ‚è±Ô∏è epoll latency in **68.75%** of threads  
  - üåê Network thread delays at same rate ‚Äî but **external RTT normal (<50ms)**  
  - üîÑ Scheduling delays in 10.1% of threads (11/109)  
  - üö® Minimal CPU impact (only 6 anomalous threads)  

> This indicates inefficiency in asynchronous event handling rather than raw CPU exhaustion.

---

## üìù **Analysis Logic** üìù

### üîß ts-config-service  
‚û°Ô∏è **Metrics first**: CPU usage rose from 37% ‚Üí 50%, but more critically, eBPF shows **79.41% of threads suffering epoll latency** ‚Äî indicating the event loop is struggling to process I/O events efficiently.  
‚û°Ô∏è Run queue delays affect over 12% of threads ‚Äî confirms **scheduling contention**, pointing to CPU as a constrained resource.  
‚û°Ô∏è Logs show **zero errors** ‚Äî rules out application crashes or exceptions.  
‚û°Ô∏è Traces reveal **high span latency (up to 65Œºs)** in config retrieval endpoint ‚Äî consistent with blocked event loops.  
‚û°Ô∏è External network RTT remains low (<50ms), so **not a network or downstream issue**.  
‚úÖ **Conclusion**: Internal CPU/event-loop bottleneck is root cause.

---

### üîß ts-order-service  
‚û°Ô∏è **Metrics first**: CPU usage jumped from 18% ‚Üí **100.5%**, a clear red flag. This aligns with eBPF data showing **run queue delays in 40% of threads** ‚Äî classic symptom of CPU starvation.  
‚û°Ô∏è Despite only one thread flagged for CPU latency, the aggregate usage suggests **compute-bound workload**.  
‚û°Ô∏è epoll and file I/O delays are side effects ‚Äî when CPU is saturated, even async operations stall.  
‚û°Ô∏è Logs show **no errors**, confirming no crash or exception path.  
‚û°Ô∏è Traces show **low-latency spans (avg 9Œºs)** ‚Äî surprisingly good, but this may reflect short-lived requests that don‚Äôt capture full processing chain.  
‚û°Ô∏è Bandwidth and disk latency increases are minor and correlated with CPU surge ‚Äî likely symptoms, not causes.  
‚úÖ **Conclusion**: CPU overload is primary; all other latencies are downstream effects.

---

### üîß ts-order-other-service  
‚û°Ô∏è **Metrics first**: CPU usage only increased from 9% ‚Üí 12.4% ‚Äî not concerning in isolation.  
‚û°Ô∏è But **68.75% of threads show epoll and network thread latency** ‚Äî highly unusual without CPU spike.  
‚û°Ô∏è eBPF shows **no file I/O issues**, and logs are clean ‚Äî no app-level errors.  
‚û°Ô∏è External RTT is normal ‚Äî rules out network degradation.  
‚û°Ô∏è This pattern suggests **inefficient event demultiplexing** ‚Äî possibly too many idle watchers, poor epoll setup, or thread pool exhaustion.  
‚û°Ô∏è Scheduling delays (11/109 threads) suggest mild contention, but not dominant.  
‚úÖ **Conclusion**: Event loop inefficiency is the core issue ‚Äî possibly code-level (e.g., blocking in event handler) or configuration-related.

---

## üí° **Recommended Actions** üí°

### üîß ts-config-service
üõ†Ô∏è **Immediate Fixes**:  
- Profile CPU usage with `perf` or eBPF tools to identify hot functions in the event loop.  
- Optimize thread pool size for I/O-bound workloads ‚Äî ensure event loop threads aren‚Äôt oversubscribed.  
- Review recent code deployments for blocking calls in non-blocking contexts (e.g., sync DB calls in async handlers).

üõ°Ô∏è **Prevention**:  
- Set up alerts for **epoll wait time > threshold** (e.g., >10ms).  
- Monitor **run queue length per pod** ‚Äî alert if sustained >1.  
- Implement CPU throttling backpressure in high-load scenarios.

---

### üîß ts-order-service
üõ†Ô∏è **Immediate Fixes**:  
- **Scale horizontally immediately** ‚Äî CPU at 100% means no headroom.  
- Use `top`, `pidstat`, or eBPF to identify which process/thread consumes CPU ‚Äî check for infinite loops or unbounded computations.  
- Review recent logic changes: look for expensive serialization, regex, or JSON parsing in hot paths.

üõ°Ô∏è **Prevention**:  
- Enforce CPU limits and requests in Kubernetes to prevent noisy neighbors.  
- Add **CPU usage >90% for 2min** alerting.  
- Consider offloading heavy computation to worker queues.

---

### üîß ts-order-other-service
üõ†Ô∏è **Immediate Fixes**:  
- Audit epoll/kqueue usage ‚Äî ensure file descriptors aren‚Äôt leaking or watchers aren‚Äôt accumulating.  
- Check thread pool configuration for event dispatchers ‚Äî may be undersized.  
- Use eBPF to trace `epoll_wait` duration ‚Äî confirm if events are processed slowly or not arriving.

üõ°Ô∏è **Prevention**:  
- Add monitoring for **event loop lag** (time between event arrival and processing).  
- Instrument event loop with metrics (e.g., active watchers, wakeups/sec).  
- Conduct code review for any **blocking operations in event handlers**.

---

## ‚úÖ **Overall Conclusion**  
All three services exhibit **internal latency due to system-level resource constraints**, primarily centered around **CPU and event processing efficiency**.  

Despite **no log errors** and **healthy external network performance**, the eBPF and metrics data reveal **deep internal bottlenecks**:

- `ts-config-service`: üîÑ **Moderate CPU + severe epoll delays** ‚Üí optimize event loop.  
- `ts-order-service`: üö® **Critical CPU saturation** ‚Üí scale and profile.  
- `ts-order-other-service`: ‚è±Ô∏è **Event loop inefficiency** ‚Üí audit epoll logic.

> üîé **Final Fault Priority**: **CPU > Event Loop (epoll) > Scheduling > File I/O**  
> üåê **Network and downstream systems are ruled out** as root causes.

üìå **Next Steps**: Prioritize CPU profiling and event loop optimization across all three services. Deploy enhanced observability for internal latency metrics beyond traditional logs and traces.
